      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8708-1" target="احكمهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (K:) and (K) <hi rend="ital">from doing that which he desired;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8708-2" target="احكمهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; and

Ibrá- heem En-Nakha'ee is related to have said,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8708-4" target="حَكِّمِ" n="4" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> اليَتِيمَ كَمَا تُحَكِّمُ وَلَدَكَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Restrain thou the orphan from acting in an evil,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a corrupt, manner, and make him good,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">virtuous, as thou restrainest thine offspring</hi> &amp;c.: and of every one whom thou preventest, or restrainest, or withholdest, from doing a thing, thou sayest, [<foreign lang="ar">حَكَمْتُهُ</foreign> and]   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8708-5" target="حكّمته" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n8708"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8708-6" target="احكمته" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: or, accord. to Aboo-Sa'eed Ed-Dareer, as related by Sh, the forementioned saying of En-Nakh'ee means <hi rend="ital">let the orphan decide respecting his property,</hi> when he is good, or virtuous, <hi rend="ital">as thou lettest thine offspring</hi> &amp;c.; but this explanation is not approved. (Az, TA.) And Jereer says, <quote>
                     <L><foreign lang="ar">أًبَنِى حَنِيفَةَ <ref cref="n8708-7" target="أَحْكِمُوا" n="7" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>سُفَهَآءَكُمْ</foreign>
                     </L>

                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">O sons of Haneefeh, restrain your lightwitted ones: verily I fear for you that I may be angry</hi>]: (S, TA:) i. e., restrain and prevent them from opposing me.                   <hi rend="ital">He made him to turn back,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">revert, from the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَكَمَ الفَرَسَ</foreign>, and

And <foreign lang="ar">حَكَمَ الدَّابَّةَ</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">الفَرَسَ</foreign>, (K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَكْمٌ</foreign>; (S; [so in my two copies of that work;]) and

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8708-12" target="حكّم" n="12" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF" select="n8708"/> الحَوَادِثَ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He controlled events:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">مُحَكَّمٌ</foreign>]. (MF.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَكَمْتُ عَلَيْهِ بِكَذَا</foreign> originally signifies <hi rend="ital">I prevented, restrained,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">withheld, him from doing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suffering, any other than such a thing, so that he could not escape it.</hi> (Msb.) [Hence it means <hi rend="ital">I condemned him to such a thing;</hi> as, for instance, the payment of a fine or of a debt, and death.] And hence, (Msb,) <foreign lang="ar">حَكَمَ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, Msb, K,) aor.

(S, KL, MA, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">حكم</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حكم</foreign>, [so in the TA, without any syll. signs, app. <foreign lang="ar">حَكُمَ</foreign> inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حُكْمٌ</foreign>,] is said of a man, signifying <hi rend="ital">He reached the utmost point,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">degree, in its meaning</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">فِى</foreign>
